  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>This issue adds a new <tt>TolerantUpdateProcessorFactory</tt> making it possible to configure solr updates so that they are "tolerant" of individual errors in an update request...</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">  &lt;processor class=<span class="code-quote">"solr.TolerantUpdateProcessorFactory"</span>&gt;
    &lt;<span class="code-object">int</span> name=<span class="code-quote">"maxErrors"</span>&gt;10&lt;/<span class="code-object">int</span>&gt;
  &lt;/processor&gt;
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>When a chain with this processor is used, but maxErrors isn't exceeded, here's what the response looks like...</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">$ curl <span class="code-quote">'http:<span class="code-comment">//localhost:8983/solr/techproducts/update?update.chain=tolerant-chain&amp;wt=json&amp;indent=<span class="code-keyword">true</span>&amp;maxErrors=-1'</span> -H <span class="code-quote">"Content-Type: application/json"</span> --data-binary <span class="code-quote">'{<span class="code-quote">"add"</span> : { <span class="code-quote">"doc"</span>:{<span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"1"</span>,<span class="code-quote">"foo_i"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"bogus"</span>}}, <span class="code-quote">"delete"</span>: {<span class="code-quote">"query"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"malformed:["</span>}}'</span>
</span>{
  <span class="code-quote">"responseHeader"</span>:{
    <span class="code-quote">"errors"</span>:[{
        <span class="code-quote">"type"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"ADD"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"1"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"message"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field <span class="code-quote">'foo_i'</span>=<span class="code-quote">'bogus'</span> msg=For input string: \"</span>bogus\""},
      {
        <span class="code-quote">"type"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"DELQ"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"malformed:["</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"message"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse <span class="code-quote">'malformed:['</span>: Encountered \"</span>&lt;EOF&gt;\<span class="code-quote">" at line 1, column 11.\nWas expecting one of:\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\n    "</span>}],
    <span class="code-quote">"maxErrors"</span>:-1,
    <span class="code-quote">"status"</span>:0,
    <span class="code-quote">"QTime"</span>:1}}
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>Note in the above example that:</p> 
                  <ul> 
                   <li>maxErrors can be overridden on a per-request basis</li> 
                   <li>an effective <tt>maxErrors==-1</tt> (either from config, or request param) means "unlimited" (under the covers it's using <tt>Integer.MAX_VALUE</tt>)</li> 
                  </ul> 
                  <p>If/When maxErrors is reached for a request, then the <em>first</em> exception that the processor caught is propagated back to the user, and metadata is set on that exception with all of the same details about all the tolerated errors.</p> 
                  <p>This next example is the same as the previous except that instead of <tt>maxErrors=-1</tt> the request param is now <tt>maxErrors=1</tt>...</p> 
                  <div class="code panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="codeContent panelContent"> 
                    <pre class="code-java">$ curl <span class="code-quote">'http:<span class="code-comment">//localhost:8983/solr/techproducts/update?update.chain=tolerant-chain&amp;wt=json&amp;indent=<span class="code-keyword">true</span>&amp;maxErrors=1'</span> -H <span class="code-quote">"Content-Type: application/json"</span> --data-binary <span class="code-quote">'{<span class="code-quote">"add"</span> : { <span class="code-quote">"doc"</span>:{<span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"1"</span>,<span class="code-quote">"foo_i"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"bogus"</span>}}, <span class="code-quote">"delete"</span>: {<span class="code-quote">"query"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"malformed:["</span>}}'</span>
</span>{
  <span class="code-quote">"responseHeader"</span>:{
    <span class="code-quote">"errors"</span>:[{
        <span class="code-quote">"type"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"ADD"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"1"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"message"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field <span class="code-quote">'foo_i'</span>=<span class="code-quote">'bogus'</span> msg=For input string: \"</span>bogus\""},
      {
        <span class="code-quote">"type"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"DELQ"</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"id"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"malformed:["</span>,
        <span class="code-quote">"message"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse <span class="code-quote">'malformed:['</span>: Encountered \"</span>&lt;EOF&gt;\<span class="code-quote">" at line 1, column 11.\nWas expecting one of:\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\n    "</span>}],
    <span class="code-quote">"maxErrors"</span>:1,
    <span class="code-quote">"status"</span>:400,
    <span class="code-quote">"QTime"</span>:1},
  <span class="code-quote">"error"</span>:{
    <span class="code-quote">"metadata"</span>:[
      <span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.common.ToleratedUpdateError--ADD:1"</span>,<span class="code-quote">"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field <span class="code-quote">'foo_i'</span>=<span class="code-quote">'bogus'</span> msg=For input string: \"</span>bogus\"",
      <span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.common.ToleratedUpdateError--DELQ:malformed:["</span>,<span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse <span class="code-quote">'malformed:['</span>: Encountered \"</span>&lt;EOF&gt;\<span class="code-quote">" at line 1, column 11.\nWas expecting one of:\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\n    "</span>,
      <span class="code-quote">"error-class"</span>,<span class="code-quote">"org.apache.solr.common.SolrException"</span>,
      <span class="code-quote">"root-error-class"</span>,<span class="code-quote">"java.lang.NumberFormatException"</span>],
    <span class="code-quote">"msg"</span>:<span class="code-quote">"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field <span class="code-quote">'foo_i'</span>=<span class="code-quote">'bogus'</span> msg=For input string: \"</span>bogus\"",
    <span class="code-quote">"code"</span>:400}}
</pre> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                  <p>...the added exception metadata ensures that even in client code like the various SolrJ SolrClient implementations, which throw a (client side) exception on non-200 responses, the end user can access info on all the tolerated errors that were ignored before the maxErrors threshold was reached.</p> 
                  <hr> 
                  <div class="panel" style="border-width: 1px;">
                   <div class="panelHeader" style="border-bottom-width: 1px;">
                    <b>Original Jira Request</b>
                   </div>
                   <div class="panelContent"> 
                    <p>Has anyone run into the problem of handling bad documents / failures mid batch. Ie:</p> 
                    <p>&lt;add&gt;<br> &lt;doc&gt;<br> &lt;field name="id"&gt;1&lt;/field&gt;<br> &lt;/doc&gt;<br> &lt;doc&gt;<br> &lt;field name="id"&gt;2&lt;/field&gt;<br> &lt;field name="myDateField"&gt;I_AM_A_BAD_DATE&lt;/field&gt;<br> &lt;/doc&gt;<br> &lt;doc&gt;<br> &lt;field name="id"&gt;3&lt;/field&gt;<br> &lt;/doc&gt;<br> &lt;/add&gt;</p> 
                    <p>Right now solr adds the first doc and then aborts. It would seem like it should either fail the entire batch or log a message/return a code and then continue on to add doc 3. Option 1 would seem to be much harder to accomplish and possibly require more memory while Option 2 would require more information to come back from the API. I'm about to dig into this but I thought I'd ask to see if anyone had any suggestions, thoughts or comments. </p> 
                   </div>
                  </div> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>

The xml file can be POSTed Solr to index via the post.jar file so you can see the output.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis patch attempts to report back to the user the following for each document that failed:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n1&gt; the ordinal position in the file where the error occurred (e.g. the first, second, etc &lt;doc&gt; tag).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n2&gt; the &lt;uniqueKey&gt; if available.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n3&gt; the error.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe general idea is to accrue the errors in a StringBuilder and eventually re-throw the error after processing as far as possible.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIssues:\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n1&gt; the reported format in the log file is kind of hard to read. I pipe-delimited the various &lt;doc&gt; tags, but they run together in a Windows DOS window. What happens on Unix I\'m not quite sure. Suggestions welcome.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n2&gt; From the original post, rolling this back will be tricky. Very tricky. The autocommit feature makes it indeterminate what\'s been committed to the index, so I don\'t know how to even approach rolling back everything.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n3&gt; The intent here is to give the user a clue where to start when figuring out what document(s) failed so they don\'t have to guess.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n4&gt; Tests fail, but I have no clue why. I checked out a new copy of trunk and that fails as well, so I don\'t think that this patch is the cause of the errors. But let\'s not commit this until we can be sure.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n5&gt; What do you think about limiting the number of docs that fail before quitting? One could imagine some ratio (say 10%) that have to fail before quitting (with some safeguards, like don\'t bother calculating the ratio until 20 docs had been processed or...). Or an absolute number. Should this be a parameter? Or hard-coded? The assumption here is that if 10 (or 100 or..) docs fail, there\'s something pretty fundamentally wrong and it\'s a waste to keep on. I don\'t have any strong feeling here, I can argue it either way....\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n6&gt; Sorry, all, but I reflexively hit the reformat keystrokes so the raw patch may be hard to read. But I\'m pretty well in the camp that you \u003cb\u003ehave\u003c\\/b\u003e to reformat as you go or the code will be held hostage to the last person who \u003cb\u003edidn\'t\u003c\\/b\u003e format properly. I\'m pretty sure I\'m using the right codestyle.xml file, but let me know if not.\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n7&gt; I doubt that this has any bearing on, say, SolrJ indexing. Would someone look this over and commit it if they think it\'s ready?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eNote to self: do NOT call initCore in a test case just because you need a different schema.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe problem I was having with running tests was because I needed a schema file with a required field so I naively called initCore with schema11.xml in spite of the fact that @BeforeClass called it with just schema.xml. That functionality would also be useful in other use cases, but that\'s another issue).  \\n\\n  NOTE: This does change the behavior of Solr. That\'s because the addCmd variable isn\'t initialized until the &lt;add&gt; tag is encountered and the NPE is a result of using the addCmd variable later (I think I was seeing it at line 118). I think it would be better to fail if the first element wasn\'t an &lt;add&gt; element rather than because it just happens to cause an NPE.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eWhile I\'m at it, though, what do you think about making this robust enough to ignore ?xml and\\/or !DOCTYPE entries? How do you feel about refactorings &lt;G&gt;? \\n\\n I got bitten by this problem again so I decided to dust off the patch, and I re-created it. This one shouldn\'t have the gratuitous re-formatting. But, after I added the bookkeeping, the method got even more unwieldy, so I extracted some of the code to methods in XMLLoader. I also have the un-refactored version if this one is too painful. \\n\\n This patch incorporates the changes you suggested months ago. I\'m a little uncertain whether putting a constant in UpdateParams.java was the correct place, but it seemed like a pattern used for other parameters. \\n\\n One minor issue: The behavior is the same here as it used to be if you don\'t start the packet with &lt;add&gt;. An NPE is thrown. That\'s because the addCmd variable isn\'t initialized until the &lt;add&gt; tag is encountered and the NPE is a result of using the addCmd variable later (I think I was seeing it at line 118). I think it would be better to fail if the first element wasn\'t an &lt;add&gt; element rather than because it just happens to cause an NPE. \\n\\n While I\'m at it, though, what do you think about making this robust enough to ignore ?xml and\\/or !DOCTYPE entries? The errors are managed by an UpdateRequestProcessor that must be added before other processors in the chain. It accepts maxErrors in the configuration as default or as a request parameter. If used, the default maxErrors value is Integer.MAX_VALUE, to get the current behavior one should set it to 0 (however, wouldn\\u2019t make sense to add the processor to the chain in this case, unless it depends on the request parameter).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThis would handle only bad documents, but not others mentioned in previous comments (like Tika parsing exceptions, etc).\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\nThe 00:26\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    This is a different approach for this issue. The errors are managed by an UpdateRequestProcessor that must be added before other processors in the chain. It accepts maxErrors in the configuration as default or as a request parameter. If used, the default maxErrors value is Integer.MAX_VALUE, to get the current behavior one should set it to 0 (however, wouldn\\u2019t make sense to add the processor to the chain in this case, unless it depends on the request parameter). \\nThis would handle only bad documents, but not others mentioned in previous comments (like Tika parsing exceptions, etc). \\nThe response will look something (ie: if maxErrors defaults to Integer.MAX_VALUE, and i send 100 docs and all 100 fail, should i really get a 200 status code back?)  \\n I think this would make it more confusing. Having this processor means that the client wants to manage failing docs on their side. If all the docs fail so be it, they\\u2019ll know how to manage it on their side, I don\\u2019t think that should be a special case. Plus, I think getting the 200 gives you more information, it tells you that Solr tried adding all the docs the client sent and it didn\\u2019t abort somewhere in the middle, like it would happen if you get a 4XX\\/5XX \\n\\n I was also thinking that this processor won\\u2019t work together with DistributedUpdateProcessor, it has its own error processing, plus the distribution would create multiple internal requests (chains too) right? Also, the ConcurrentUpdateSolrServer used in SolrCmdDistributor would batch docs in a non-deterministic way, right? Would be impossible to count errors at this level.               \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-13974667\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-445?focusedCommentId=13974667&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-13974667\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"hossman\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_13974667_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=hossman\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"hossman\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Hoss Man\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - Once all those assertions were passing, then I changed it to use 5 nodes, 2 shards, 2 replicas and started testing all of those scenerios against 5 HttpSolrClients pointed at every individual node (one of which hosts no replicas) as well as a ZK aware CloudSolrClient. class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOk, i\'ve been going around in circles on this issue for the past few weeks, but i\'ve finally got something that feels like progress.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eListing everything new since the last patch would be fairely tedioius, so i\'ll focus on the broad strokes...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003epunting on deletes (for now)\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethe previuos processDelete method was totally broken in distributed queries (was doing equality comparisons of Strings directly to enum objects, made assumptions about \u003ctt\u003eisLeader\u003c\\/tt\u003e pased on previous \\\"add\\\" commands in the same request, etc...)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ei was having enough time struggling with getting adds to work properly, that i just removed the delete code completely\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ebased on the rest of the progress (see below) re-adding support for deletes should be straight forward, but will require some refactoring of how the errors are tracked &amp; counted to distinguish between an \\\"add doc w\\/id=22\\\" that fails and a \\\"delete doc w\\/id=22\\\" that fails in the same request\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eDealing with forward(ing\\/ed) requests and async distributed failures\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eMost of the meat of the test failures in the last patch came from dealing with the async requests fired off my\u003cbr\\/\u003e\\n\u003ctt\u003eDistributedUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e and how to deal with failures reported by other leaders.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eI started down the road of trying to do a bettter job in \u003ctt\u003eSolrCmdDistributor\u003c\\/tt\u003e of tracking the \u003ctt\u003eUpdateCommand\u003c\\/tt\u003e that corisponds with each \u003ctt\u003eReq\u003c\\/tt\u003e so that when processing the \u003ctt\u003eError\u003c\\/tt\u003e we could know what failed remotely &#8211; this code is still in the patch (because i think it\'s cleaner then the \u003ctt\u003ecmdString\u003c\\/tt\u003e tracking currently in Solr) but proved mostly useless because of how \u003ctt\u003eConcurrentUpdateSolrClient\u003c\\/tt\u003e can combine multiple \\\"requests\\\" together.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eThe next step, which mostly worked, was to improve the error handling in DUP\'s \u003ctt\u003efinish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e so that instead of aborting with info about whatever (remote) Error happened to return first, it now returns a new \u003ctt\u003eDistributedUpdatesAsyncException\u003c\\/tt\u003e which wraps &amp; remembers the summary info of all the remote errors encountered &#8211; or at least, all of the errors that were previously candidates to tell the user about.  Stuff that was swallowed &amp; logged before is still swallowed &amp; logged.\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eOne notable change her is that i switched \u003ctt\u003eDUP.finish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e from directly calling \u003ctt\u003eSOlrQueryResponse.setException()\u003c\\/tt\u003e and instead made it throw the exception.  Independent of this issue, the existing behavior seems like a bug \\/ bad-form &#8211; what if the caller already caught some earlier exception it wants to return and \u003ctt\u003efinish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e is just being called in finally?\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eThis lead me to discover \u003ca href=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/browse\\/SOLR-8633\\\" title=\\\"DistributedUpdateProcess processCommit\\/deleteByQuery call finish on DUP and SolrCmdDistributor, which violates the lifecycle and can cause bugs.\\\" class=\\\"issue-link\\\" data-issue-key=\\\"SOLR-8633\\\"\u003e\u003cdel\u003eSOLR-8633\u003c\\/del\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e &#8211; the patch from that issue is currently including in this patch because it\'s so neccessary for hte current code.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eFWIW: if, for some reason, folks think calling \u003ctt\u003eSOlrQueryResponse.setException()\u003c\\/tt\u003e is better for some wacko reason, then \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcess.finish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e could, in theory, go check \u003ctt\u003eSOlrQueryResponse.getException()\u003c\\/tt\u003e and treat it the same way as exceptions it catches (see below) but that\'s a lot more tedious and (and error prone in the long run)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eOnce \u003ctt\u003eDUP.finish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e started throwing \u003ctt\u003eDistributedUpdatesAsyncException\u003c\\/tt\u003e, tracking all the various errors we care about from distributed requests became possible...\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e now pays attention to when the request is a \u003ctt\u003eTOLEADER\u003c\\/tt\u003e forwarded request, and if so:\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eit acts tolerant of up to \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e failures (just like single node)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ein \u003ctt\u003efinish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e, if \u003cb\u003eany\u003c\\/b\u003e failures happened, return the first error &#8211; and annotate it with info about \u003cb\u003eall\u003c\\/b\u003e the failures in this request, using the existing \u003ctt\u003eSolrException.getMetadata()\u003c\\/tt\u003e map.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eConcurrentUpdateSolrClient\u003c\\/tt\u003e already ensures that if a \u003ctt\u003eSolrException\u003c\\/tt\u003e happens on the remote server, any \\\"metadata\\\" included in the response for that exception is copied into the local \u003ctt\u003eSolrException\u003c\\/tt\u003e it constructs\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eSo if\\/when \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor.finish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e catches a \u003ctt\u003eDistributedUpdatesAsyncException\u003c\\/tt\u003e, it loops over the wrapped exceptions, and pulls out the metadata for each of those to update it\'s list of known failures\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ewhich error is returned if \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e exceeded: now the \\\"first\\\" one\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ei mentioned this above in discussing how async errors from other leaders are handled, but i wanted to emphasis it and elaborate a bit\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ein the original patch, exceptions were \u003cb\u003ecompletley\u003c\\/b\u003e ignored until \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e were seen, at which point hte next exception was immediately (re)-thrown\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethat made sense for single node cases, but in a distributed case, with async exceptions, we can\'t always just \\\"rethrow\\\" an exception\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eit\'s also ambiguious what the \\\"last\\\" exception really is in an async situation.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eso now, instead,  \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e always remembers the \u003cb\u003efirst\u003c\\/b\u003e exception it caught, and if\\/when \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e is exceeded, it re-throws that first exception\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003elater, in \u003ctt\u003efinish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e that (remembered) exception is annotated with metadata about \u003cem\u003eall\u003c\\/em\u003e the failures\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethis metadata is critical for forwarded requests, but should also be useful for \u003ctt\u003eSolrClient\u003c\\/tt\u003e users who (should) see it copied into a \u003ctt\u003eRemoteSolrException\u003c\\/tt\u003e even if they don\'t get the normal \u003ctt\u003eUpdateResponse\u003c\\/tt\u003e object and it\'s \u003ctt\u003egetResponseHeader()\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethis, in my opinion, makes the behavior of using \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e more useful (and consistent with how stock solr works) when there is a fundamental problem with your data &#8211; you get an error indicating the \u003cem\u003efirst\u003c\\/em\u003e problem document in your data, as opposed to seeing an error from the 11th, or 101th, or \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors+1\u003c\\/tt\u003e malformed document in your data.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eif folks disagree, we just need to re-work the \u003ctt\u003eFirstErrTracker\u003c\\/tt\u003e class to be a \u003ctt\u003eLastErrTracker\u003c\\/tt\u003e class...\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eFirstErrTracker.throwFirst()\u003c\\/tt\u003e becomes \u003ctt\u003eLastErrTracker.throwLast()\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003einstead of checking \u003ctt\u003enull == first\u003c\\/tt\u003e, \u003ctt\u003eLastErrorTracker.caught(Throwable)\u003c\\/tt\u003e would ignore any additional exceptions once \u003ctt\u003etrue == thrown\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ethe problem with returning \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e (and \u003ctt\u003enumDeletes\u003c\\/tt\u003e if we want that)\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003egetting \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e to work correctly in a distributed request is really hard\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ecurrently the code (specifically on the first node processing the \u003ctt\u003eAddUpdateCommand\u003c\\/tt\u003e just requires that \u003ctt\u003esuper.processAdd()\u003c\\/tt\u003e succeeds to do \u003ctt\u003enumAdds++\u003c\\/tt\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethis gives a missleading number when the failures aren\'t reported immediately because they were forwarded async to a diff leader and we only find out about problems in \u003ctt\u003efinish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eeven if we only did \u003ctt\u003enumAdds++\u003c\\/tt\u003e for docs where we know we are the leader, getting the count from \u003cem\u003eother\u003c\\/em\u003e leaders later is tricky\\n\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eright now, the only way \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e learns the results of any async requests to other leaders is if \u003ctt\u003eDUP.finish()\u003c\\/tt\u003e throws an error &#8211; we can get \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e from the metadata of those errors, but that doesn\'t help the case when requests succeed\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eDUP\u003c\\/tt\u003e doesn\'t currently do anything with successful responses, so there\'s no easy way to get the numAdds in that \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e from this feature, focus solely on being tolerant and reporting the errors (which we can do accurately)\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eif people want to know how many succeeded, they can use features like \u003ctt\u003eversions=true\u003c\\/tt\u003e explicitly &#8211; although even then, i\'m not sure if it will work reliably today ... i don\'t see any indication that DUP merges the remote responses when that feature is used.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003emake \u003ctt\u003eversion=true\u003c\\/tt\u003e to get the info from requests we forward to, and prune the response down to just a simple \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e count in finish()\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003esame problem as above if i\'m correct about \u003ctt\u003eversions=true\u003c\\/tt\u003e not currently handled correctly in forward(ing\\/ed) requests\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ereturn distinct \u003ctt\u003enumAddsAttempted\u003c\\/tt\u003e and \u003ctt\u003enumAddsConfirmed + new jira\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003egeting \u003ctt\u003enumAdds\u003c\\/tt\u003e (or \u003ctt\u003enumDeletes\u003c\\/tt\u003e) count in the responseHeader really feels like it should be an orthoginal feature to being tolerant of \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ewe should open a distinct issue to track adding that as a feature, and ensuring that DUP aggregates correctly from all the various leaders that requests get forwarded to\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethis is waht i personally think we should do &#8211; notably because it would make it trivial to know how many documents you added when streaming a bunch of data, even if you \u003cb\u003edon\'t\u003c\\/b\u003e use this update processor.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003ethe nuance of the \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors=N\u003c\\/tt\u003e param\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ei just want to point out &#8211; in a distributed cloud setup, there is no way to truely enforce a hard limit at \u003ctt\u003emaxErrors\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ethe async processing means that if a request includes docs destined for diff shards, we can\'t ensure that \u003cb\u003eonly\u003c\\/b\u003e that max amount of errors will be hit &#8211; we might hit more errors in async threads before we notice and stop processing\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ei don\'t think this is a problem, it\'s a feature of handling updates to diff shards\\/leaders in paralel, but it does mean we might want to rethink the param name ? (\u003ctt\u003eerrorTolleranceThreshold=N\u003c\\/tt\u003e perhaps?\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThere\'s still a lot of work todo, in no particular order...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003edeletes\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eneed to refactor the way we track errors (both locally and stashed in the SolrException metadata) so that we can we can distinguish \\\"add doc w\\/id=22\\\" faiulres from \\\"delete doc w\\/id=22\\\" failures\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eprobably need to rethink the \u003ctt\u003eresponseHeader\u003c\\/tt\u003e formatting for how errors are tracked as well in order to distinguish them\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eonce we have that, adding a \u003ctt\u003eprocessDeletes(...)\u003c\\/tt\u003e method that works similar to processAdd should be trivial\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eneed to beef up the cloud testing to include delete checks\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eCloudSolrClient\u003c\\/tt\u003e\\n\\t\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003eall of the tests using \u003ctt\u003eCloudSolrClient\u003c\\/tt\u003e currently fail because of how that client does it\'s own \\\"direct to leaders\\\" splitting\\/merging of docs destined for diff shards.\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\\t\u003cli\u003ea bunch of new code needs written there (may be able to refactor\\/share some stuff from the error list merging code in \u003ctt\u003eTolerantUpdateProcessor\u003c\\/tt\u003e (see above about refactoring that for deletes)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\t\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eneed lots more randomized testing\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003etons of nocommits that need cleaned up\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"hossman\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_15135274_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=hossman\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"hossman\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Hoss Man\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15135274_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'05\\/Feb\\/16 23:41\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-02-05T23:41:42+0000\'\u003e05\\/Feb\\/16 23:41\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Ok, i\'ve been going around in circles on this issue for the past few weeks, but i\'ve finally got something that feels like progress. \\n\\n Listing everything new since the last patch would be fairely tedioius, so i\'ll focus on the broad strokes... \\n\\n \\n\\t punting on deletes (for now)\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t the previuos processDelete method was totally broken in distributed queries (was doing equality comparisons of Strings directly to enum objects, made assumptions about  isLeader  pased on previous \\\"add\\\" commands in the same request, etc...) \\n\\t\\t i was having enough time struggling with getting adds to work properly, that i just removed the delete code completely \\n\\t\\t based on the rest of the progress (see below) re-adding support for deletes should be straight forward, but will require some refactoring of how the errors are tracked &amp; counted to distinguish between an \\\"add doc w\\/id=22\\\" that fails and a \\\"delete doc w\\/id=22\\\" that fails in the same request \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t Dealing with forward(ing\\/ed) requests and async distributed failures\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t Most of the meat of the test failures in the last patch came from dealing with the async requests fired off my \\n DistributedUpdateProcessor  and how to deal with failures reported by other leaders. \\n\\t\\t I started down the road of trying to do a bettter job in  SolrCmdDistributor  of tracking the  UpdateCommand  that corisponds with each  Req  so that when processing the  Error  we could know what failed remotely &#8211; this code is still in the patch (because i think it\'s cleaner then the  cmdString  tracking currently in Solr) but proved mostly useless because of how  ConcurrentUpdateSolrClient  can combine multiple \\\"requests\\\" together. \\n\\t\\t The next step, which mostly worked, was to improve the error handling in DUP\'s  finish()  so that instead of aborting with info about whatever (remote) Error happened to return first, it now returns a new  DistributedUpdatesAsyncException  which wraps &amp; remembers the summary info of all the remote errors encountered &#8211; or at least, all of the errors that were previously candidates to tell the user about.  Stuff that was swallowed &amp; logged before is still swallowed &amp; logged.\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t One notable change her is that i switched  DUP.finish()  from directly calling  SOlrQueryResponse.setException()  and instead made it throw the exception.  Independent of this issue, the existing behavior seems like a bug \\/ bad-form &#8211; what if the caller already caught some earlier exception it wants to return and  finish()  is just being called in finally? \\n\\t\\t\\t This lead me to discover   SOLR-8633   &#8211; the patch from that issue is currently including in this patch because it\'s so neccessary for hte current code. \\n\\t\\t\\t FWIW: if, for some reason, folks think calling  SOlrQueryResponse.setException()  is better for some wacko reason, then  TolerantUpdateProcess.finish()  could, in theory, go check  SOlrQueryResponse.getException()  and treat it the same way as exceptions it catches (see below) but that\'s a lot more tedious and (and error prone in the long run) \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t Once  DUP.finish()  started throwing  DistributedUpdatesAsyncException , tracking all the various errors we care about from distributed requests became possible...\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t  TolerantUpdateProcessor  now pays attention to when the request is a  TOLEADER  forwarded request, and if so:\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t it acts tolerant of up to  maxErrors  failures (just like single node) \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t in  finish() , if  any  failures happened, return the first error &#8211; and annotate it with info about  all  the failures in this request, using the existing  SolrException.getMetadata()  map. \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t  ConcurrentUpdateSolrClient  already ensures that if a  SolrException  happens on the remote server, any \\\"metadata\\\" included in the response for that exception is copied into the local  SolrException  it constructs \\n\\t\\t\\t So if\\/when  TolerantUpdateProcessor.finish()  catches a  DistributedUpdatesAsyncException , it loops over the wrapped exceptions, and pulls out the metadata for each of those to update it\'s list of known failures \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t which error is returned if  maxErrors  exceeded: now the \\\"first\\\" one\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t i mentioned this above in discussing how async errors from other leaders are handled, but i wanted to emphasis it and elaborate a bit \\n\\t\\t in the original patch, exceptions were  completley  ignored until  maxErrors  were seen, at which point hte next exception was immediately (re)-thrown \\n\\t\\t that made sense for single node cases, but in a distributed case, with async exceptions, we can\'t always just \\\"rethrow\\\" an exception\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t it\'s also ambiguious what the \\\"last\\\" exception really is in an async situation. \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t so now, instead,   TolerantUpdateProcessor  always remembers the  first  exception it caught, and if\\/when  maxErrors  is exceeded, it re-throws that first exception\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t later, in  finish()  that (remembered) exception is annotated with metadata about  all  the failures\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t this metadata is critical for forwarded requests, but should also be useful for  SolrClient  users who (should) see it copied into a  RemoteSolrException  even if they don\'t get the normal  UpdateResponse  object and it\'s  getResponseHeader()  \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t this, in my opinion, makes the behavior of using  TolerantUpdateProcessor  more useful (and consistent with how stock solr works) when there is a fundamental problem with your data &#8211; you get an error indicating the  first  problem document in your data, as opposed to seeing an error from the 11th, or 101th, or  maxErrors+1  malformed document in your data. \\n\\t\\t if folks disagree, we just need to re-work the  FirstErrTracker  class to be a  LastErrTracker  class...\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t  FirstErrTracker.throwFirst()  becomes  LastErrTracker.throwLast()  \\n\\t\\t\\t instead of checking  null == first ,  LastErrorTracker.caught(Throwable)  would ignore any additional exceptions once  true == thrown  \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t the problem with returning  numAdds  (and  numDeletes  if we want that)\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t getting  numAdds  to work correctly in a distributed request is really hard \\n\\t\\t currently the code (specifically on the first node processing the  AddUpdateCommand  just requires that  super.processAdd()  succeeds to do  numAdds++ \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t this gives a missleading number when the failures aren\'t reported immediately because they were forwarded async to a diff leader and we only find out about problems in  finish()  \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t even if we only did  numAdds++  for docs where we know we are the leader, getting the count from  other  leaders later is tricky\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t right now, the only way  TolerantUpdateProcessor  learns the results of any async requests to other leaders is if  DUP.finish()  throws an error &#8211; we can get  numAdds  from the metadata of those errors, but that doesn\'t help the case when requests succeed \\n\\t\\t\\t  DUP  doesn\'t currently do anything with successful responses, so there\'s no easy way to get the numAdds in that case \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t possible solutions...\\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t eliminate the concept of  numAdds  from this feature, focus solely on being tolerant and reporting the errors (which we can do accurately)\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t if people want to know how many succeeded, they can use features like  versions=true  explicitly &#8211; although even then, i\'m not sure if it will work reliably today ... i don\'t see any indication that DUP merges the remote responses when that feature is used. \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t make  TolerantUpdateProcessor  detect when it\'s not a leader for something, and in that case  implicitly  add  version=true  to get the info from requests we forward to, and prune the response down to just a simple  numAdds  count in finish()\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t same problem as above if i\'m correct about  versions=true  not currently handled correctly in forward(ing\\/ed) requests \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t return distinct  numAddsAttempted  and  numAddsConfirmed  values &#8211; probably not as useful to end clients, but more accurate representation of what we know...\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t track a distinct \\\"numAddsAttempted\\\" for  every  shard we forward to (added together at end of request)\\n\\t\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t\\t kind of a sketchy pain in the ass to do \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t assume  numAddsConfirmed = numAddsAttempted  for any other shard leader we dont see an exception from \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t for shard leaders we do get exceptions from, add to our numAddsConfirmed based on the metadata (ie:  numAddsConfirmed + remoteException.getMetatata(NUM_ADDS_CONFIRMED)  \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t treat it as a distinct feature in a new jira\\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t geting  numAdds  (or  numDeletes ) count in the responseHeader really feels like it should be an orthoginal feature to being tolerant of  maxErrors  \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t we should open a distinct issue to track adding that as a feature, and ensuring that DUP aggregates correctly from all the various leaders that requests get forwarded to \\n\\t\\t\\t\\t this is waht i personally think we should do &#8211; notably because it would make it trivial to know how many documents you added when streaming a bunch of data, even if you  don\'t  use this update processor. \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t the nuance of the  maxErrors=N  param\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t i just want to point out &#8211; in a distributed cloud setup, there is no way to truely enforce a hard limit at  maxErrors  \\n\\t\\t the async processing means that if a request includes docs destined for diff shards, we can\'t ensure that  only  that max amount of errors will be hit &#8211; we might hit more errors in async threads before we notice and stop processing \\n\\t\\t i don\'t think this is a problem, it\'s a feature of handling updates to diff shards\\/leaders in paralel, but it does mean we might want to rethink the param name ? ( errorTolleranceThreshold=N  perhaps? \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n \\n\\n\\n\\n There\'s still a lot of work todo, in no particular order... \\n\\n \\n\\t deletes\\n\\t \\n\\t\\t need to refactor the way we track errors (both locally and stashed in the SolrException metadata) so that we can we can distinguish \\\"add doc w\\/id=22\\\" faiulres from \\\"delete doc w\\/id=22\\\" failures \\n\\t\\t probably need to rethink the  responseHeader  formatting for how errors are tracked as well in order to distinguish them \\n\\t\\t once we have that, adding a  processDeletes(...)  method that works similar to processAdd should be trivial \\n\\t\\t need to beef up the cloud testing to include delete checks \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t  CloudSolrClient \\n\\t \\n\\t\\t all of the tests using  CloudSolrClient  currently fail because of how that client does it\'s own \\\"direct to leaders\\\" splitting\\/merging of docs destined for diff shards. \\n\\t\\t a bunch of new code needs written there (may be able to refactor\\/share some stuff from the error list merging code in  TolerantUpdateProcessor  (see above about refactoring that for deletes) \\n\\t \\n\\t \\n\\t need lots more randomized testing \\n\\t tons of nocommits that need cleaned up \\n \\n             \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=hossman\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_15193606_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'14\\/Mar\\/16 16:44\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2016-03-14T16:44:25+0000\'\u003e14\\/Mar\\/16 16:44\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    (ment to post last friday but was blocked by the jira outage) \\n\\n Ok ... i think things are looking pretty good on the jira\\/  SOLR-445   branch &#8211; good enough that I\'d really like some help reviewing the code &amp; sanity checking the API (and internals for anyone who is up for it)... \\n\\n \\n\\n For folks who haven\'t been following closely, here\'s what the configuration looks like (from the javadocs)... \\n\\n  \\n   &lt;processor class= \\\"solr.TolerantUpdateProcessorFactory\\\" &gt;\\n    &lt; int  name= \\\"maxErrors\\\" &gt;10&lt;\\/ int &gt;\\n  &lt;\\/processor&gt;\\n \\n  \\n\\n When a chain with this processor is used, but maxErrors isn\'t exceeded, here\'s what the response looks like... \\n\\n  \\n $ curl  \'http: \\/\\/localhost:8983\\/solr\\/techproducts\\/update?update.chain=tolerant-chain&amp;wt=json&amp;indent= true &amp;maxErrors=-1\'  -H  \\\"Content-Type: application\\/json\\\"  --data-binary  \'{ \\\"add\\\"  : {  \\\"doc\\\" :{ \\\"id\\\" : \\\"1\\\" , \\\"foo_i\\\" : \\\"bogus\\\" }},  \\\"delete\\\" : { \\\"query\\\" : \\\"malformed:[\\\" }}\' \\n {\\n   \\\"responseHeader\\\" :{\\n     \\\"errors\\\" :[{\\n         \\\"type\\\" : \\\"ADD\\\" ,\\n         \\\"id\\\" : \\\"1\\\" ,\\n         \\\"message\\\" : \\\"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field  \'foo_i\' = \'bogus\'  msg=For input string: \\\\\\\" bogus\\\\\\\"\\\"},\\n      {\\n         \\\"type\\\" : \\\"DELQ\\\" ,\\n         \\\"id\\\" : \\\"malformed:[\\\" ,\\n         \\\"message\\\" : \\\"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse  \'malformed:[\' : Encountered \\\\\\\" &lt;EOF&gt;\\\\ \\\" at line 1, column 11.\\\\nWas expecting one of:\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\\\\n    \\\" }],\\n     \\\"maxErrors\\\" :-1,\\n     \\\"status\\\" :0,\\n     \\\"QTime\\\" :1}}\\n \\n  \\n\\n Note in the above example that: \\n\\n \\n\\t maxErrors can be overridden on a per-request basis \\n\\t an effective  maxErrors==-1  (either from config, or request param) means \\\"unlimited\\\" (under the covers it\'s using  Integer.MAX_VALUE ) \\n \\n\\n\\n If\\/When maxErrors is reached for a request, then the  first  exception that the processor caught is propagated back to the user, and metadata is set on that exception with all of the same details about all the tolerated errors. \\n\\n This next example is the same as the previous except that instead of  maxErrors=-1  the request param is now  maxErrors=1 ... \\n\\n  \\n $ curl  \'http: \\/\\/localhost:8983\\/solr\\/techproducts\\/update?update.chain=tolerant-chain&amp;wt=json&amp;indent= true &amp;maxErrors=1\'  -H  \\\"Content-Type: application\\/json\\\"  --data-binary  \'{ \\\"add\\\"  : {  \\\"doc\\\" :{ \\\"id\\\" : \\\"1\\\" , \\\"foo_i\\\" : \\\"bogus\\\" }},  \\\"delete\\\" : { \\\"query\\\" : \\\"malformed:[\\\" }}\' \\n {\\n   \\\"responseHeader\\\" :{\\n     \\\"errors\\\" :[{\\n         \\\"type\\\" : \\\"ADD\\\" ,\\n         \\\"id\\\" : \\\"1\\\" ,\\n         \\\"message\\\" : \\\"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field  \'foo_i\' = \'bogus\'  msg=For input string: \\\\\\\" bogus\\\\\\\"\\\"},\\n      {\\n         \\\"type\\\" : \\\"DELQ\\\" ,\\n         \\\"id\\\" : \\\"malformed:[\\\" ,\\n         \\\"message\\\" : \\\"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse  \'malformed:[\' : Encountered \\\\\\\" &lt;EOF&gt;\\\\ \\\" at line 1, column 11.\\\\nWas expecting one of:\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\\\\n    \\\" }],\\n     \\\"maxErrors\\\" :1,\\n     \\\"status\\\" :400,\\n     \\\"QTime\\\" :1},\\n   \\\"error\\\" :{\\n     \\\"metadata\\\" :[\\n       \\\"org.apache.solr.common.ToleratedUpdateError--ADD:1\\\" , \\\"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field  \'foo_i\' = \'bogus\'  msg=For input string: \\\\\\\" bogus\\\\\\\"\\\",\\n       \\\"org.apache.solr.common.ToleratedUpdateError--DELQ:malformed:[\\\" , \\\"org.apache.solr.search.SyntaxError: Cannot parse  \'malformed:[\' : Encountered \\\\\\\" &lt;EOF&gt;\\\\ \\\" at line 1, column 11.\\\\nWas expecting one of:\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_QUOTED&gt; ...\\\\n    &lt;RANGE_GOOP&gt; ...\\\\n    \\\" ,\\n       \\\"error-class\\\" , \\\"org.apache.solr.common.SolrException\\\" ,\\n       \\\"root-error-class\\\" , \\\"java.lang.NumberFormatException\\\" ],\\n     \\\"msg\\\" : \\\"ERROR: [doc=1] Error adding field  \'foo_i\' = \'bogus\'  msg=For input string: \\\\\\\" bogus\\\\\\\"\\\",\\n     \\\"code\\\" :400}}\\n \\n  \\n\\n ...the added exception metadata ensures that even in client code like the various SolrJ SolrClient implementations, which throw a (client side) exception on non-200 responses, the end user can access info on all the tolerated errors that were ignored before the maxErrors threshold was reached. \\n\\n CloudSolrClient in particular &#8211; which already has logic to split  UpdateRequests ; route individual commands to the appropraite leaders; and merge the responses &#8211; has been updated to handle merging these responses as well. \\n\\n (The  ToleratedUpdateError  class for modeling these types of errors has been added to solr-common, and has static utilities that client code can use to parse the data out of the responseHeader or out of any client side SolrException metadata) \\n\\n \\n\\n There are still a bunch of  nocommit  comments, but they are almost all related to either: \\n \\n\\t adding tests \\n\\t adding docs \\n\\t refactoring \\/ hardening some internal APIs \\n\\t removing suspected unneccessary \\\"isLeader\\\" code (once tests are final) \\n \\n\\n\\n I\'ll keep working on those, but I\'d appreciate feedback from folks on how things currently stand. \\n\\n Even if you don\'t understand\\/care about the internals, thoughts on the user facing API would be appreciated.
